Chapter XXXIX.
Of the extraction of bloodsucking attached to the throat.
When the bloodsucker is medicated with what we have said in the division of the cure with medicines and does not confer, consider then in the throat of the patient to the sun, because you may have compressed the tongue of him with the instrument which to you we have recommended.
Therefore, if you see the bloodsucker, extract that with a small pin or with a subtle gesture decently.
And if it is not possible to extract with that, then take a concave cannula and introduce that into the throat of the patient, and then place in the concavity of the cannula a burning iron, and do this so many times (until the bloodsucker is dead and is removed from the throat), and abstain the patient all day of water.
And then press a vessel full of cold water, and work the mouth of him in that, and wash the mouth with that; and do not swallow any of that and bad the water an hour after with his hand, because the bloodsucker as soon as it feels the water catches.
But if it is not forcibly ejected by what we have recommended, then fumigate the patient with cimet or with asafoetida by the instrument which we have recommended in the fumigation of the uvula.
Do this, so long as it falls.
And there is another way of operation in the fumigation of that, which is that you take a bowl in which there are burning coals and the bowl is covered with a cover in the middle of which there is a hole, and it is composed in that hole the extremity of the instrument; and then let the fumigation descend; and place the patient's mouth on the extremity of the cannula, and close his mouth so that the fumigation is not forcibly ejected until you know that the fumigation has reached the bloodsucker, because the bloodsucker immediately falls.
And if it does not catch, then you repeat the fumigation many times, and abstain the patient from drinking, and eat salty and dry causes, and do not drink water, and thus it is necessary that with this regimen it be forcibly ejected.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the bloodsucker of the throat is treated when it is seen; and it is similar to forceps as you see, unless that in it there is some curvature: which is placed in the throat, and the extremity of it is similar to the beak of a stork, which is gaunt, in which it is sharpened with a file, so that, when compressing any cause, it does not let go.
Chapter .xl.
In which is the sum of the sermon concerning abscesses and their incision.
Abscesses are special matters, of many kinds, according to the remembrance of them, of each one in this book.
And they are diverse in perforation and incision of them by two ways, of which one is by the species of abscesses in themselves; and by that which we comprehend of the humidities.
And the second way is according to the places where they occur in the body, for the abscess that occurs in the head is different from the abscess that occurs in the buttocks; and the abscess in the fleshy place is different from the abscess that occurs in the joint; and to each of them is its own treatment by operation.
And more than abscesses are some which ought not to be perforated but rather when the maturation of the flesh in them or the completion of them.
There are other abscesses which ought to be treated when they are ripe, and not when they are mature according to their completion, just as abscesses that are near the joints, for when an abscess occurs near a joint, its being is prolonged until it can pour out what is in its circuit, and very soon those ligaments or nerves of that joint are corrupted, because it is the cause of contraction of that limb; or it is an abscess near a major limb, and if you delay the perforation of it before its maturation, it will damage the major limb; or it is near the buttocks, therefore perforate it before it is mature; and you ought not to perforate it cru, of incomplete digestion, but that which is near the buttocks, so that you cannot pierce the preon of it and it be elongated to the parts of the buttocks, and a fistula be made, or that it be done in the term of it that it not be healed. But more, you ought to know the hour of the perforation of the abscess, and thus it is when it is mature.
And you ought to know that it is mature when it is the cessation of pain and the cessation of fever, and towards the diminution of the heat and the pulse, and the sharpness of the head of the abscess, and the other signs.
And that you ought to know the perforation to be done in the place furthest from the abscess and of pus coming from the cure of the eminence.
And perforation always be by the length of the flesh or the body, if the abscesses are in the parts of the arms or the feet, and in the places of the tendons, of the nerves, of the arteries; and, afterwards, in all places equal in which there is no reflection; for in those that are reflected, use of perforation according to that limb.
But when the abscess is in a fleshy place, then it is best that you let the perforation of it until its digestion is confirmed according to completion, as we have said; for if you perforate it before that, it is prolonged the course of the pour of it and of much filth, and very soon the lips of it are hardened and the depth of it.
But some abscesses are perforated according to the width of the flesh or the body of necessity, or according to what the limb requires.
And you ought to administer small perforation, and in large abscesses large perforation and many sections according to the variety of the greatness of the abscesses.
And others are of abscesses in which the codpiece ought to be concave and be incised, when it is done so that bread is made and it is done in a term that it already follows, just as those that occur in trops of buboes.
And of those are those that are incised with a section having three angles; and of those is the one in which it is incised like the figure of a myrtle leaf, just as the abscesses of the angles.
And of them are those in which a round section and a lunar section are administered, and similar to those.
But that one to whom there is no such as his abscesses are superficial, you ought to perforate that with superficial perforation, or flat only.
And you ought when the abscess is large and has already collected much pus, that you perforate it and do not take that you extract all the pour in that hour; having extracted from it one part, and then close the abscess until the next day, and then extract a larger part, and then do that many times according to gradation until it is fully drained.
And more so if the patient is of weak virtue, or pregnant woman, or small child, or old in decrepitude, for the animal spirit many times is resolved with the egress of the pus, and very soon the patient dies, and you operate on them.
Therefore, guard this chapter with great care, and in the way in which you perforate these abscesses, you ought to abstain from the plagues and consider therefore if the plague of the abscess is few, or a flat section, then you administer the qualms of it or of a counter-coction; and if the abscess is large, and the fissures of the perforation are many, then you ought to put a meca in each tract until they reach together.
And if in the abscess is abscinded a part of the codpiece or has concaved that in the circuit, then you ought to cover it with old coction or with a thread made of cloth of it, as when you have treated loaves or rags, its humidity; and strengthen that within the third day; and then process that and cure it with that which ought of the dressings until it is healed.
But if blood flows during the operation, then you administer cold water and wine to which you have wrung a cloth, and place it over the place of the blood flow many times.
But if the blood flow persists, then you must administer regimen and cure as I have recommended in many places in this book of ours and of division.
But if it is in wintertime, and the place of the abscess is a place of many nerves, then you must enfund  powders in wine and caut oil, and place those on the place.
And if it is in summer, and the places are fleshy, then you must place powders soaked in water and oil or in wine and oil, and all that be cold until the third day, as we have said, and then you must untie the abscess and cleanse it and administer to it that which is fitting for its cure until it is healed.
And thus is that which is necessary of the knowledge of the cure of abscesses universally, but according to the way of distinction I have already said of every abscess in what manner is the way of its cure by chapters singularly.
Chapter .xli.
Of the incision of abscesses that come in the nape of the head.
In the nape of the head, small abscesses, and they are of a kind of nodes that contain tunics that are to their making; and the kinds of them are many.

And sometimes there are some of these abscesses that are in the head in some men with which of all there is no humidity; the cause is because I incised upon an abscess in the head of an old woman and retrieved the abscess as if it were a hard, rough, white, thing which could not be drained, and if anyone was struck with that, it would plague them.

Chapter .xlii.

Chapter .xliii.
Of the section of the pile of the abscess that happens within the throat.
The ancients said this section in the throat, and no one in our land has done it.
And this is the inscription of the sermon of those.
But in men having a squint, cover that the extraction of the throat be avoided, as for that it is not done well for because all the veins and the largest of the body are here.

And Albucasis says that the sum of the sermon which we have recommended, the exposition is no more than seeing that some of these abscesses have already opened the throat of the patient, and the patient has come into death, and the skin of it is dried, and some go to cut the epiglottis so that the patient breathes over the place of the wound by some respiration, and be saved from death.

Chapter XLIV.
Of incision over the abscess which occurs in the throat outside, and is called hernia of the throat.

Chapter XLV.
Of incision of the kinds of nodes.
Of nodes there are many kinds, and I have already said all the kinds of them in the division.
And I must recount thus the difference between a node and an excrescence as if making a doubt.
Therefore I say that in an excrescence there is heat and fever and vehement pain until the boiling of the superfluity is settled; and it is complicated putrefaction that at the hour the fever, the pain, and the heat cease.
But in a node there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it counts that which is in the sac, which is in the u sac properly.
And it is according to the color of the body, and the beginning of it is like a seed and it is made thus as a vase, whether it is larger or smaller, and they are according to two kinds, whether they are fatty and contain humidity, and the colors of the humidity are many, according to what I said in the division.
Therefore, when you come to the cure of a node, that you examine it and inquire into it at the beginning with the instrument that is called intromes, according to what will come its form in the chapter which is near this.
And the manner of inquiry of abscesses and of all nodes, and it is that you take this instrument and introduce it into the place most humid which you find in the abscess, and you revolve your fingers with that little by little until you know that the instrument has already penetrated the cord.
And then finally your hand according to the measure of the greatness of the abscess, and then you extract the intromes and consider what is emitted in the trace of it.
And if the humidity is flowing out, of whatever color it may be, then you incise it with a superficial incision according to what I have said in the other abscesses.
And if from the trace of the intromes there is no humidity, then you know that it is fatty.
And dry over it with an incision having the shape of a cross according to this form: as you are taught, and suspend that with forceps, and excise the cord from all parts with ease, and keep the skin or sac, if you can, over it and extract that sania with the node.
But if it is ruptured in the operation, it is not possible to extract that sania, and many times it should be so, and then you extract it in pieces until nothing of it remains.
For if anything of it remains, little or much, the node returns according to the most.
And if you see that any small part of it remains, then fill the wound with some corrosive powders sharp and strengthen the wound, and place over it a cautery, and cure it with the other cure until it is healed.
And if it is a large node, then you stitch the two lips of it and cure it with what encases.
But if a pulsatile vein is in it, or non-pulsatile, then you coat and moisten the place with a thrice-strained vinegar that is vitriol, and leave that strait for two or three days until you can stitch the wound and that the boiling of the blood is calmed; and then return to incise what is broken of the node.

Chapter XLVII.
Of the cure of the nipples of men which are assembled from women.

Chapter XLIX.
Of the incision of abscesses that occur by artery or vein.
When an artery is ruptured, and the chain which is above it is consolidated, then many times abscesses occur. And the signs by which it is known that inflammation and abscess are by the artery or vein: that when an abscess is by artery it is long aggregated in the forefront of the body; and that when you press the abscess with your fingers, you feel in it that which is stridor.
And that which is by vein is round and manifest of the body.
And incision on this abscess is an error, and most of all in that which is below the armpits, and in the angles, and in the neck, and in most places of the body; and it is a great one, therefore it is commanded that its cure with iron should be avoided, and that which is in the extremities, or on the head, it should be avoided.
But on that which is of those by inflammation of the orifice of the artery, split it in the chain with a long section; and then break the section with hooks and then the artery, and deliura of the tunics until it is uncovered.
And then put on that needle and make it penetrate into the other part, and tighten the artery with a double thread in two places, — which cause you to yeen see in the extraction of two arteries which are in the temples.
And then prick the place which is between two ligaments with a spatula until there is all the blood in it, and it is dissolved the abscess.
And then administer a cure in which is engendered power until the ligaments fall; and then cure that with suitable washes to it until it is healed.
And if it is an abscess by the section of a vein, then it is commanded that you have with your hand that which is possible of the abscess with the chain, and then introduce the needle below the place which you have had below your hand, and make it penetrate; and be in that double thread until you extract that from the other part, and then ligua the abscess with a good ligament according to as I have told you in the ligament of uva4 of two parts with two extremities of the thread.
But if you fear that the thread will be extracted, then introduce the thread with that needle below all the abscess, and then make the incision of the first needle, and tighten your threads in four places.
Then dry the abscess in the middle place of it until when it is issued that which is in it, then you should split the superfluity of the chain, and leave that which of it is tied.
And then place on it the powder which you have submerged in wine and oil, and then administer the cure which is made with calx and unguents while it is healing.
Chapter 1 of the abscess which happens due to twisting of nerves.
Thus as abscesses occur in arteries and veins, and similarly abscesses occur in nerves when they are struck or caused by excessive work, and by similar means.
And it is made most in the places of the armpits or the ankle, or in any place where the joints are sore.
And it is a severe abscess, and it is assembled to the color of the other body, and in the majority of its dispositions there is a sense of it, and when it is squeezed with violence, the patient feels a sensation of stupor.
And it is not an abscess that is added in the front of the body, and for this reason the chain is left, and it is sore to every part and does not go to the parts in front or behind.
Therefore those that are in the joints should not be enclosed with iron, because very quickly it will cause contraction.
But those that are in the head or on the forehead,  should be enclosed with a spatula. But if it is a small abscess, then you should take it with the forceps and cut it from the root.
And if it is large, then you should suspend it with a hook, and scrape it, and then cover it; and adjust the patch with sutures, and cure it until it is healed.
Chapter .li.
Of the section of an abscess which happens from a boil that happens to the belly.
And it happens to some men, growths in the bellies of those and in other parts of the body of those, the ones that are called fungals because of their similarity to those with fungi, of those whose root is subtle and the head of it is thick; and already the lips of those are turned, and it is of those that are small, and it is of those that are greatly magnified.
And I have already seen one, and in the belly of him there were two parts that were more like fungi, and there was no difference between those white, of fine root.
And already the lips of those were turned and were opening, and humidity ran from it all the time.

Chapter .lxi.
On the extraction of a stone from women.

Chapter lxii.
On the incision of a hernia.
Hernia ayguoza is nothing but an accumulation of moisture in the white membrane which is below the codena of the genitals containing the huou, and is called ciphac.
And some times it is in the proper panniculus which has prepared it nature in the part of the huou, before it is known that there is another huou; and it is the codena of the genitals between the white membrane which we have said, and it is not that but tart.
And the generation of this hernia is due to weakness which happens to the genitals, because into those it is poured this matter, and sometimes it happens by percussion made upon the genitals.
And this moisture is having many colors, for the color of it is either declining to citrine or sanguine, or red, or it is black and mucous, or it is aqueous white, and this is the most common.
And the signs by which it is known that this accumulation of water is there are: for if it is in the white membrane which we have said, then the abscess is round declining a little in length as if it were the figure of a huou, and appears the genitals, for the moisture contains that from all parts.
And if the moisture is in the proper panniculus, then the abscess is round in the part of the huou and by this it is estimated that it is another huou.
And if the moisture is between the codena of the genitals and the white membrane, then it feels below the centiment.
And as you want the knowledge of the color of the moisture, then you try the color of the moisture in the abscess with an introme that is inserted into the cavity of which the shape is preceded; and according to what is seen in the vestige of the introme, judge of that which is inside of it.
Therefore, when we come to the cure of him with iron, then we command the patient to be fleubotomized if this is possible, and sometimes we purge his bowels.
And then have him lie on his back on some cause a little higher, and place some warm cloths over him.
And then sit you on the left side of him, and command the minister to follow on the right side of him, the one extending his arm to one of two sides to the groin of the genitals and to the parting of the navel of the belly.
And then take a broad spatula and split the groin of the genitals from the middle place for the length into the proximity of the pubic bone.
And let the section be made according to the rectum, equally distant from the line that divides the skin of the genitals, until it reaches the white ciph, comprehending.
And scrape that, and observe, and guard yourself so that you do not cut that; and your excoriation with which you excoriate by a wide partition that it may be suspended with the most and subtly examine with the excoriation according to the quantity as much as possible.
And then perforate the white ciph full of water with a wide perforation, and extract all the water.
And then separate between the two labia of the section with a hook, and extend the ciph to the upper parts; and do not touch the groin comprehending, and incise the ciph in that manner that is to your possible. And incise that with its totality or in pieces, and mostly its subtle side, for if you do not scrutinize exquisitely the incision of it, it is not done with certainty that the water does not return.
But if the humor proceeds from that outside of its groin in the hour of your operation, then when you will have completed the section of the ciph, return deint that, and then adjust the two labia of the groin of the genitals with suture, and then cure that as with other plagues, until it is healed.
And if the humor is corrupted by another malady, then you must lie the vessels which are sore on the suspensory, and extract the humor, and then cure that with the water that we have said.
But if the water is aggregated in two parts at once, then you know that two are the hernias; therefore incise that partition according to that you have done in the other equally; and if it is to your view that it be an operation, then you do it.
And then you abstergiys the blood, and introduce into the sections wool submerged in oil or in rose oil; and place before another wool which you have submerged in wine and oil, and expand that over the genitals and the navel of the belly; and place above doubled cloths and powders, and lie those above with a ligament which is according to this form:
And then be taken the cloths and be humplitz of carded wool according to this semblance; and be made the extremities with which it is pressed of cloth or of wet wool, and be added with structure in the braguier of the breeches, and one of the extremities presses from the buttock into the two, and the second presses at the parting of the pubic bone, and two extremities over two thighs of below and two other extremities over two hipbones, and all structure be adjusted in the braguier of the breeches.
And some times this hernia is medicated artificially with cautery in place of section with iron; and it is that you take a subtle cutellar cautery and that you incise with that the groin of the genitals, and it is ignited according to that we have recounted until it be discovered the white ciph containing the water, and then you take cautery according to this form: and it is assembled like a Greek letter.
And then perforate with that ciph, and it is ignited until all the humidity be thrown out.
And then extend the ciph with hooks, and scrape with hooks, and scrape with a subtle cautery ignited; and incise that according to that is to your possible until you eradicate all of it; and guard yourself of the humor that the fire does not touch it.
And know that this operation is more saving and more distant from the flux of blood, and better than operation with section.
But if to you there is contrariety abscess caut in the hour of section or in the hour of cautery, or flux of blood, then you must cure that contrariety that it does to you for that, with cure the which convenes to him according to that is said.
But if the patient is fearful, and does not wait for the second operation for its horror, then administer perforation according to that we have recounted here; and it is when it is certified you must, for that which we have said of the significations, that that hernia is aqueous.
Then you must make the patient lie on some elevated cushion, and then perforate the abscess in the lowest part of it with a broad spatula, and place the perforation according to the length of the body.
And let the aperture be wide until all the water runs out.
And then place on the spot cloth and lie that and leave that, so that it runs the remaining of the water. And then cure that until the plague is healed.
But if contrariety is in the emission of the water in that hour you perforate that: and this is not done except for that because the white pannicol in the orifice of the plague makes contrariety and prohibits the eyssiment of the water, then you must put in the plague pain or instrument with which is extracted the water of the hydropitz, the form of which is preceded; or adjust in the opprecio of the plague a little.

Chapter .lxiii.
Of the section on fleshy hernia and its cure.
Know that in the section on this hernia, there is fear of losing it to harm in the major dispositions; for to me it has been seen the dismissal of it and being saved by that better.
And you are remembering the operation on that and the species of the abscesses.
Therefore, I say that the abscesses arise in the bodies of those whose genitals are composed and this is done for many causes: or by excess acute aggravation, which is poured into the genitals, or by percussion.
And the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body, and it is not aggravated in pain, and the abscess is severe.
And very much the abscess is petrified, of which the color is dark, and there is no feeling in it.
And sometimes it is done by the knotting of the arteries, and by the inflation of those so that already the memory of it is perceived, or by the inflation of veins.
But that which is by the inflation of arteries is known by the dispersion of the abscess when you compress it with your fingers; and no cove that you touch it.
But that which is done by the inflation of veins is not dispersed by it any cause of the compression with the fingers.
And it is already possible that on this species a section is made and on the other flesh; and that you insert the blade of the genitals, and then extend the fluid to the parts below, and extract that from the white cup, and deliver the suspensory of the vessels, and tie them, and inscise the suspensory as much as you deliver that from all parts of the fluid.

And if there is adhesion for any cause of the cup, or between that which is between the vessels, then you must deliver all that adhesion and inscise it by a round incision.
But if it is the birth of flesh in the place of the adhesion which is behind, then you must inscise all that which is of it, and extract the fluid as we have said.
Therefore, as the operation is completed, then fill the wound with wool infused in rose oil and wine; and then cure it with the other cure until it is healed.

Chapter .lxv.

Chapter .lxix.
Of castration.
Know that castration in our law is excused, but for the cause it is lightly remembered to me that I remember it in this book; and it is not necessary the remembrance of it unless for two ways, of which one is so that it is in the science of the physician when he is interrogated about it, that he knows the cure of it to whom it happens; and the other way is that we many times have need of castration of other animals for our benefits for them, as for goats, and sheep, and pigs, and similar to the animals.
And therefore I say that castration is done in two ways: either by attrition, or by fissure to section.
But in that which is done by attrition, the way of the operation is that we make the beast to be cezer in warm water until its genitals are softened and are limp and that they hang. And then take those with your hand until they are resolved and do not appear from the touch.
But in castration done by fissure and section, when you have the beast and press the groin of its testicles with your left hand.
And then lie the suspensory, and cut over each wound with a section between two wounds processed.
And then cut those that you will have each excoriated. And do not leave on those of the bandage any cause, but the subtle bandage which is over the veins.
And this manner of castration is better the one done by attrition, for attrition strongly leaves no cause of the testicles for which the beast desires coyt.
And then cure the wound until it is healed.

But in women it is a species: and it is that the cunh of the woman over the pental is as if two testicles of a man, a little of all diminished at the front part as if the perpucii of a man and two testicles.
And the cure is of three species: of two of the men and of one species of the women. And it is that when you cut those flesh adjusted until it escapes the imprecio of it, and then that you cure those with the cure of the other plagues.
And in the second species of men of which you see urine which is in the groin of the testicles, there is no cure nor operation in it.

Chapter .lxxii.
Of the cure of alratica.
Alratica is when the cone of the woman is not perforated, or is the small tract. And it is natural or accidental.
Accidental is due to illness that preceded, and that is made either by flesh not well adjusted or by a subtle or thick cyph.
And it is made either in the front of the mother, or in the ribs of her, or in the upper part of her, or in the lower part of her, and prohibits coitus and pregnancy and childbirth, and very much prohibits menstruation.
And the knowledge of that is made by examining the metrona, if the oppilacio is apparent, properly; but if it is not apparent, then you search for it with your fingers or with the ray.
But if the oppilacio is by a subtle cyph, and it is proper to the two labia, then you cut and disrupt that.
And it is that you put powder on the two labia, and then place your fingers indicated from both the hands at once.
And the woman be on her back, her thighs extended, and then extend the two labia with force until that subtle cyph is broken and the oppilacio is open.
And then take wool and soak it in oil and put that on the location, and wash with water every day so that the cut location is not consolidated.
But if the cyph is thick and thick, then when you cut that with a spatula or a myrtle leaf.
But if the oppilacio is by flesh, then suspend that with linen, and cut that.
And be with you the medicines that make cease the flow of blood by biting, such as ahacatia, and dragon's blood, and incense, adjusted with album of egg.
And then administer a wide lead pipe so that the plague is not consolidated slightly.
And keep that for some days and administer calgua of the lime.
And then be cured with the other cure of consolidation until it is healed.
And sometimes it happens in the mother's nativity of other flesh, and then when you cut according to this manner. But if this is by a carbuncle, to the carbuncle the which is in the mother be not made contrariety with iron in any manner.

And count those, whether they be multiplied, one after the other, and they are separated by the head, distinguish those between the ligament in the umbilical cord of each of them, and sometimes they are born thus as if it were one fetus by gentle natural insertion, and sometimes they are born by a less praiseworthy insertion, as we have recounted.
And if some of them are difficult in childbirth and arrive at what we have said of unnatural figures, then take care of them as we have recounted.
And if the midwife is skillful and does what is done with ease and subtlety, and with slowness, and is ingenious according to every figure according to what is prepared for her by the engineer, bringing to health.
Remembrance of that which is formed in the womb from embryos and miscarriages.
Sometimes they are formed in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and sometimes ten, and it has already been verified that one woman aborted six, and another gave birth to ten, the cause of which was made by the measurement of the glorious wise men.
And all this is covered that it should be in the science of the midwife, as it is very close to that appearance of this, and therefore it is paused at that which is covered.
Chapter .lxxvi.
Of the extraction of the fetus when it is dead.
When you cure the dead fetus with what we have said in the division of the medication and it is not outside, and you are forced to use surgery with your hand, then consider if the woman is of sound virtue and is not among those accidents by which she is feared to be harmed.
Then consider that the woman be laid on her back upon her two, and her head be inclined downwards and her thighs be elevated.
And the minister has that of two parts or be tied on the bed so that the body of him does not extend during the extraction of the fetus.
And then you moisten the mouth of the mother of him with humid oils and with mucilage of althea and of fennel and of its seed.
And then the midwife anoints her hand with those oils and mucilages, and then introduces her hand with facility into the mother, and then seeks with the hand in the place where the hooks are in the fetus.
And convenient places in this: therefore you consider if the fetus is prepared that descends upon its head, and then you place the hooks in its heels, or in the neck, or in the mouth, or in the palate, or below the beard, or in the fork of it, or in the places proper of the back, or below the hypochondria.
But if the descent is upon the feet of it, then in the pentalin, or in the middle of the back.
And consider that you have the hook in your right hand, and place the curvature of it in that place which is between the fingers of your left hand, and introduce your hand with facility and place the hook in one of those places which we have said, until you reach the left cause.
And then pause and place in the opposite position of it another hook, or the third if it is necessary, so that the traction be equal, and not be extension according to its rectum only.
And be careful to every part, so that the insertion of it be alleviated as it is done during the extraction of it.
And consider in it that which is between them that the extension be softened; and if any part of it is retained, then consider that the midwife anoints some of her fingers with oil and introduces those skillfully and revolves with those that are retained.
Therefore if the part of the fetus is born, then the hooks are changed into the place which is more out; and do so until the whole fetus is born.
But if the hand is outside the other, and it is not possible to reduce it by the constriction of it, then consider that a cloth be enveloped over it; and then extract it until the whole is born, and incise it either at the junction of the hand or in the groin.
And thus consider that you do in the other hand and in the two feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or there is an accident to it constriction in the insertion, or there is in the head of it water adjusted, then consider that you introduce between the finger spines and split the head and extract the water, or which discards this with an instrument which is named “alundat”, the form of which will come with the forms of the other instruments in the chapter which is next.
And similarly, if the bone is of great size by nature, and then the one that is inflamed, or that is swollen as we have said, then extract the bone with forceps.
And if the head is extracted and is constricted at the collarbone, then it is split so that the moisture which is in the feet is poured out.
But if it is not complicated, nor obeys this way, then you cut the head as soon as it is possible to you.
And if the bowels of the belly are festering or are in it hydropic, then you must perforate that so that the moisture that is in it runs out.
But if the feet are on its feet, then the traction of it is lighter and the direction of it to the mouth of the mother is lighter.
But if it is constricted, you must pull the belly and the foot, then you must extract that which you have enveloped on your hand, and that you split the belly and the foot so that the water that is in those runs out.
But if the other members are held and the head is turned, then the midwife puts her left hand in; but if the mouth of the mother is open, then she puts her hand in the perineum of the mother, and searches with that the head, and pulls that into the mouth of the mother, and then puts in it a hook, or two hooks, and pulls it with those.
And if the mouth of the mother is constricted by an abscess, the cautery which happens to the one, then it must not be trebled on it;  it is better that you administer effusions of humid fatty causes. And administer plasters; and follow the patient in waters that soften and moisten.
And if the feet are on its side, then if possible, it is to be pricked; and it is to be administered water as we have said in the living fetus.
And if that is not possible, then it is to be incised in pieces, and it is to be extracted.
And you must not leave any cause of the second one.
And as you have completed all your operation, then administer water as we have said of the cure in the abscesses which happened to the mother.
And if there happens a flux of blood, then you send them down in styptic waters and administer the other cure.
And I have already seen a woman in the belly of which was a dead fetus, and then over that fire another pregnancy, and then a dead fetus is the other. It happened to one a long time ago an abscess in his navel; and it inflated so that a fire opened, and he began to throw out pus.
And I was called to the cure of him, and I medicated him for a long time, and the plague did not consolidate.
Then I placed on him some causes of plaster of strong traction, and extracted from him a bone, and then after a few days, I extracted another bone; and I was too amazed, as in the belly there were no bones.
And then I thought that they were of the bones of the dead fetus.
Therefore, I continued to treat the abscess, and extracted from him more bones, the woman existing in her usual dispositions, and already living in that manner for a long time, curing him of a little bit of pus.
And I do not affirm that this is strange, but that in this there is science and help to what the physician artifices with his hand for the cure administers.
Of the forms of the instruments that are necessary to extract the fetus.
Form of the vulva with which the mother is opened:
This is the form of the vulva in which the lips are brought together, to which bringing together there are two vulvas in two extremities of two parts. But however, this vulva must be more subtle of strictori, and be made of either wood or stick of boy.
And it is the width of each stick that is two fingers and the margin of each one that is one finger, and the length of each one is one palm and a half; and in the middle place of the two sticks there are two adjustments of that same stick, which are already made, of which the length is the majority of one palm and a little more, and the width of each one is two fingers, or a little less.
And these two additaments are inserted into the mouth of the mother so that it is opened with those when you revolve the two prescribed vulvas.
Another form similar to that more subtle and lighter:
It is made of sticks of wood or boy according to the resemblance of forceps. But however, at the extremity of it there are two additaments as often, and the length of those additaments is about one palm, and the width of each one is two fingers.
And as you want with those to open the mother, then you make the woman lie on the sheet with her feet hanging, open that which is between her thighs. And then open your hand with the instrument as you do with forceps, similarly according to the quantity that you want of the opening of the mouth of the mother, until the midwife makes it so that you want.
The form of vertigo which the ancients say:
The form of impelling which is driven by the feet:
The form of dizziness which is contained in the great head:
And it is assembled like forceps, which has teeth at the extremity, sometimes, and sometimes it is made long like forceps according to this form, sometimes, which has teeth like those of a saw with which it is incised and contained. The form of dizziness little:
The form of a nail having a spine:
The form of a nail having two spines:
The form of a spatula having two extremities with which the head is cut off:
The form of two broad spatulas:
All those instruments are exercised, and when more are multiplied the species of that and are prepared by the artificers, as much as it is lighter to their operation and more useful to men for their quantity.
And in the works of those instruments, whatever they may be, you should always be prepared, because the need for them is not excusable.
Of the extraction of the second (tooth).
When the second tooth is retained, the infant should be commanded to hold his breath, and then do that  stirring with the condition, and strengthen your hand over his mouth and over his nostrils, and if by this means it is pushed out, it is good.
And if not, then you take an olla and pierce a hole in the cover and place in that herbs inside the mouth of the mother, such as calamint and rue and anise and chamomile and Arabic siccated and cinnamon and  santuary. All these herbs or some of them should be submerged in water in the olla, and place that on the fire.
And then place a tube of cane in the mouth of the mother, and keep that inside until the vapor comes to the cavity of the mother.
And then do that stirring as we have said, and the second tooth will be ejected with velocity.
But if this cure remains and it is not ejected, then you command the midwife to submerge her left hand in sesame oil or in a mixture of altea, and then introduce that into the mouth and caress with that the second tooth, and when she has found it, then take it and extend it little by little. But if it is annexed in the gum of the mother, then introduce her hand as we have recounted, and when she has found the second tooth, extract it little by little according to rectum so that the mother does not feel the violent traction. So that it may be changed on the right and left sides with ease.
And if the mouth of the mother is narrow, we have already recounted the cure with stirring and with medication of the olla with herbs.
But if it is not ejected with all the causes which we have recounted, then guard that you do not fatigue yourself on that in iteration of extraction, but rather that what is ejected from it to the mouth of the mother lies on the cloth of the woman, and then sterilize that with ointment and tetrapharmacon; for that will make it rot a little after a few days and it will be dissolved and it will be ejected.
But when it may be possible, it is raised from it evil odor to the head, and to the stomach, and that is what you read to the patient; and therefore it should be administered sub-fumigations and conveniences according to that.
But some of the Ancients already are praised sub-fumigation of narcissus and dried figs.
The form of an instrument with which the woman is sub-fumigated of the retention of menstruation and of the second tooth:
It is made of copper or of iron.
And it is placed the fine extremity in the mouth and the wide extremity over the fire, and the sub-fumigation is placed over the embers of the fire.
And keep that inside until that sub-fumigation is consumed and iterate another.
Of the cure of the unperforated anus of the child.
Many children are born and the anuses of them are not perforated, which are already subtle and opaque. Therefore it is necessary for the midwife to perforate with her finger that opaque; and if not, perforate that with a sharp spatula, and guard that it does not touch the  sphincter.
And then place on that wool infused in wine and oil; and then cure that with ointment until it is healed.
But if you fear that it will be opaque again, then place in the hole a tube for many days, and remove it when the child will want to defecate.
And already accidences opacity of the anus by consolidation of plague or of abscess; therefore it is necessary that that consolidation be incised, and then it be cured with that which we have said of the cure and of the lead.
Of the cure of fistulas that end up in the anus.
The fistulas that develop in the area below the navel and have a thickness and consistency that develop near the anus or in the space between the buttocks.
And it is a fistula or a lump.
And with that swelling being ancient and running from the humid white moisture or a subtle pus, and sometimes from these fistulas some penetrate.
And those that penetrate are known by what is emitted from them by the exit and by the windiness; and sometimes the patient uses the exit, and very often it is emitted from these worms.
And sometimes from these fistulas, they penetrate into the bladder and into the meat of the vagina; and from these penetrating ones they enter the junction of the thigh and into the notch of the hip.
And in which it is known that a fistula penetrates into the anus and does not penetrate, is that you put your finger inside the anus, and you introduce a subtle probe of wax or iron into the fistula when there is no roughness.
But if there is roughness, then introduce into that a subtle probe of lead or horsehair until you feel the probe or hair in your finger.
And if you do not feel that at all, nor do you proceed from the tract any cause of excretion or worms or windiness, thus as we have said, then you know that it is non-penetrating, and then you turn to the cure.
And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the vagina, then the significance of it is the emission of urine from it and the prohibition of it so that the place with medicine may be consolidated.
But if it is penetrating into the junction of the thigh or into the hip and causing pain in the circuit, then the sign of it is that the probe enters here if there is no roughness into the hip, and causing pain in the circuit of the part; and that from it there is pus always; and that it does not work in that medication, nor is it consolidated with an enema.
And in all those penetrating fistulas, there is no cure of all, and the cure of those is the work and vanity of the medical leaves upon which they are based.
But in that which is not penetrating and not ancient, a cure with iron is expected according to what I will tell you, and what I have already said and proved.
And it is that the patient lies between your hands on his two and raises his legs onto them, the thighs inclined towards his belly, and then introduce a probe of lead, or wax if there is roughness in the fistula, until you know the place where the probe enters.
And if that feels the patient around the anus, then cover that while you introduce your finger inside the anus.
And if you feel in your finger the probe already by itself entering uncovered, or another thing that you feel between your finger and that skin or flesh, then you know certainly that that is penetrating; and therefore do not work on that, for it is not in that cure, as we have said.
But however, some say that it is cured in some men tart.
And of the medication by which is expected benefit in it is that you ignite a subtle cautery according to the size of the fistula, as it is preceded, and introduce that ignited one into the fistula until it reaches around the anus; and then repeat that two or three times until you know that all those flesh adjusted to the fistula, which are like the quill of a bird's feather, are already cauterized.
And then cure that with poultices enveloped in border until they can all those flesh that are cauterized, and then cure that with medicines the flesh engendering and consolidating, and if it is healed, well is; and if not, then it is not healed in any time by any other cure.
And if the probe enters, and does not penetrate into your finger which is in the anus, and between that and the probe which is veiled flesh or skin, and sometimes the fistula in the place where it touches the surface of the skin, then dry the skin from the beginning of the fistula, and you see drying with the probe, and in the fistula until the drying reaches the place where the extremity of the probe reaches, and by the probe is liberated and catched.
And then purify those fistulous flesh which are assembled to the quill of a bird's feather and do not remain from those any cause.
But if flux of blood sometimes comes between you and your operation when you are inserting those flesh, then the best that may be and of the lighter pus instrument is cauterize with fire or with acute medicine, for cauterizing with fire adjusts good two habits: it is the cauterization of those flesh adjusted, and the abscessing of the blood, the drying of the humidities.
And then cure that with poultices enveloped in border or in a caus trissat until the place gets braced, and then cure the plague with enemas of hard flesh engendering and consolidating.
And so medicines in which there is styptication and drying; when then it is restored it is already healed and you do not fear iteration.
But if the fistula already reaches into the preon of the anus and is elongated from it to the surface of the body, then introduce your finger into the anus and inquire with that.
And therefore if you feel the probe and between you and it is veiled skin or flesh, and is proper to penetration, then it is not operation in it but according to your trust and of hope.
This cause is administered to him in one of three ways: either cauterize that as we have said; or to drain that while you obtain the concavity of it so that it is possible for you to introduce the instruments and the proper cure; and do not proceed with the incision so that you do not injure the ligament containing the gut, and that it may occur over the patient as if it were the will of the deity; and then cure him with that which we have said that is very strong; or elongate that veil and drain the pus that dries that within the buttock, as we have said, or with a probe or another instrument of sharp extremity, and then drain those carbuncles that are in the incision within the one where you can make the peroration; and then strive to make the restoration of the whole wound with incision, and if the orifice of pus above is not consolidated, and the fistula remains open in the part of the buttock, and pus flows lightly through the patient. And in some cases the fistula is finished in this way: it is when you introduce the probe into the fistula, and it is in the latz of the buttock around the surface of the body with the codena and on the margin of the buttock, then take a probe of perforated extremity, which is like a needle for preparing the hearts according to this form:
And introduce it into that faithful envelope of v fiels or around them; and then introduce the probe with a faithful in the fistula until you obtain the concavity of it.
But if it is penetrating in the margin of the buttock proper, then you extract the probe from that track so that you introduce your finger into the buttock; and extract the extremity of the probe and adjust the two extremities simultaneously, and tighten each one, and leave it for a day or two, and when you have incised the probe into the flesh, tighten well that within which those carns are incised that are between the two extremities of the probe and that they join.
And then cure the wound until it is consolidated and healed.
But if the orifice of the fistula is not penetrating, then make that penetrate, in whatever way it is prepared for you, but not in the preon, because it is not for you to do this so that you do not injure the ligament; and then make it with that which is healed.
The form of the spatum spinos with which the fistula is fended: the curvature of which is very acute and the other part is not acute, so that you do not injure what is not necessary, as sometimes.
Of suture of hemorrhoids in which blood flows in the incision of those.
Hemorrhoids are according to two ways, because they are between the buttock seeming like that of coals, or that those are like the fat of rasim. And of those are small and large, and that the blood flows from those always and is one, and are many, and are outside the buttock, and in the extremities of it.
But however those that are outside the buttock are according to the few humidity, of which flows clear water or a little blood with a continuous body, and are according to the color of the body.
And the cure of those that are inside the buttock is that you command the patient to lie down and that he expresses himself until the buttock is empty and the hemorrhoids appear to you. Then you take and suspend with hooks or whatever you have those with your nail, and then you introduce those of their roots.
But if the hooks are not held in those because of the humidity of them and their softening, then take those with rough cloth or with a stick or with a fleece of wool, and extract those with your fingers, and then introduce those and pulverize over them some powders caudas near the incision, so that they may be adhered to those in place of cauterization; or cauterize those according to what is preceded in the chapter of cauterization. And then cure those with the other cure until they are healed.
And if the buttock does not obey the egress, then christenize the patient with a crister in which the bite is small, and wash it with that water that is in the buttock and that obeys the egress slightly when the patient expresses himself.
But if the hemorrhoids are outside the buttock, then the cause of them is lighter, and it is that you take those with your nail, or that you take those with a hook, and introduce those, and then cure those with the water that we have said until they are healed.
And that which you have incised, cover that you administer suture of them according to this way: take a faithful envelope and introduce it into a needle and then extract the hemorrhoids to the upper parts, and make that penetrate with the needle into the root of the other part, and envelop the two extremities of the faithful in the part below the needle, and so longitudinally; and tighten the hemorrhoid with a strong structure, and then untie the faithful and extract the needle.
And do this to all, and leave one of those and do not sew it, so that the superfluity of the blood flows from that.
And then place over the buttock cloth soaked in rose oil or in cerot; and place that over the buttock and command the patient to rest. And then leave that until it heals; and when it is healed, cure those with unguents or with another cure until it is healed.
And since old ones are not useful in that medicine, then when you treat those with the point of a spatula or your fingernail until they are moist and the pus is removed from them, which prevents them from consolidating; and then treat them when they are consolidated.
Then you treat those with a vigorous scraping of pus, the first one when blood is drawn and they are excoriated; and then treat them when they are healed.
Know that a boil, it is clear, and it is not if not a red nodule according to the color of the body resembling a keycap, and it is made in all the body and mostly in the parts below the feet and in the armpits, and therefore by those pains you must treat the boil.
And therefore, when it is incised that which is in the circuit of the boil, and it is held with the forceps or a pincer, and it is eradicated from its root; and then treat that.
And if you wish, cauterize the following as it is preceded in its chapter.
But warts are small, rough, fistulous round eminence on the surface of the body, and often come in the most of the children.
And the cure of them is that you extend and incise that, or you tighten that with a thread or a needle until it comes out. And if you wish, cauterize that, according to what we have said, with fire or with a sharp medicine.
But a nettle is a small, rough, or fistulous eminence on the surface of the body that goes into the skin, and when the ant touches that it is felt in it like a bite of an ant, and it is made all over the body.
And the cure of that is that you take a tube of feather of hawk or of vulture, and it is strong, and you place that over the nettle until you contain it the circle of the tube of the parts of it; and then you revolve your hand with the tube until you incise that which is in the circuit of the nettle, and you place that in the skin of the flesh, and that you eradicate the nettle from its root.
And if you wish, do that with a tube of iron or of steel according to this form:
Let the upper part of the tube be drawn to a subtlety, blunt (so it is not perforated), enveloped so that on the finger where you apply it, it be blunted and the revolution of that.
And if you wish, cauterize the nettle according to what is said before in the cauterization of the boil in the chapter of cauterization.
On the form of the instruments that are administered to give a cure.
Sometimes a cauterizer is made of silver or of latten or of iron melted or hammered; and sometimes it is made of those instruments small and large according to those to whom they are administered, because that which is administered in the cure of the small children be small; and of those whose handles are bent or sore, the cauterizers of those be small.
The form of a large and few cauterizer:
The head of the tube of it upwards where the pouch is tied be wide according to this manner; and be to it distinction the one where the pouch is tied as often.
And the extremity of it lower, which is inserted into the handle, be blunt (so it is not opened) much like a lion, drawn to a subtlety; and in one of the sides of it be two holes, and in the other side one hole, and be the width of the hole according to the thickness of the rays and a little thicker.
And be the pouch in which are placed the medicines of bladder of beast or of sheepskin, and the root of it be a palm.
And be perforated by many holes as it is revolved; and if the space which is between the holes the thickness of the finger.
And then insert into those holes a strong thread of thread cru which be of ten threads, or about those; and adjust with that the pouch; and when it is placed in it the pouch, be straight in the head of the cauterizer between two distinct ones with a strong constriction, and then cauterize with that each hole: But the quality of cauterizing with that is that you fill the pouch with the medicine, which be heated according to the quantity of the tolerance of the patient; and guard yourself that it be not too hot nor too cold.
And then the patient be laid on his back, and elevate his legs up and place under him a cushion on which already are the men or a bolster; and then anoint the extremity of the cauterizer with oil or with egg white or with mucilage of fennel or of similiar; and then insert that into the handle with facility, and the minister presses the pouch and expresses that with two hands and at the same time with vehemence until it be evacuated in the pouch all that which is in the cauterizer; and then extract the cauterizer and the patient raises his legs to the wall.
And if the medicine forces that ayessement, keep it as much as you can; and if you sleep with that for a whole night, it is more useful in the cure.
But if you encounter a patient with a solution of the belly and its expulsion, then repeat the cautery until it heals.
And if in the anus there are hemorrhoids or suppurating abscesses, then be the cautery subtle and lion, of the cauteries with which the children are cauterized.
Of the cure of the plagues.
And I have already said in the division of the cure of the plagues what was convenient to the free, and I say so the cure of those with my hand and with medicines according to the complement.
Therefore I say that the plagues are diversified according to what in which the plagues are made and according to the place on which the plagues fall.
And the causes for which many times the plagues are made are such as a bite of a serpent, or incision of a sword or of a knife, or percussion with a lance, or with a club, or with an arrow, or similar to those of many causes.
But the plagues that are in the places of the body are such as a plague that falls on the head, or the neck, or the feet, or the belly, or the thigh, and similar to those of the limbs.
And I am recounting the cure of some plagues so that you pause that reasoning and rule over the other plagues.
And I will begin with the plagues of the head simple, for the remembrance of the composed will come to the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore I say that when a simple plague occurs in the head and it is not a fracture, then consider: if it is by a bite of a serpent or similar, and the wound has already been cleaned and it is a large plague and you fear about that patient having an abscess, then you cauterize and perform cephalic phlebotomy immediately, and do not delay this; and extract from that of the blood according to the quantity of its virtue, if no other cause prohibits phlebotomy, especially if the blood that is extracted from the plague is little.
And let the phlebotomy be on the opposite side of the plague; and guard the patient from repletion and from wine and from coarse food.
But if by any cause phlebotomy is prohibited, then let the food be lessened and do not approach to meat nor to wine.
And place on the plague, if an abscess occurs cauterize it, coat infused in rose oil or in wine in which is steeped.
But if it is certain of an abscess cauterize it, then place on the plague, if it is recent with its blood and the air has not yet changed that powder which I will recount a little later.
And if the air has already changed that, then place on the ulcer until it is healed.
But if the plague is large or is by incision of a sword and similar, and the lips of it are not adjusted by sutures, then adjust those with sutures according to how I will recount of the sutures of them.
But if the plague is already discovered from the bone and tendon, and there is no retention of it but a small suspensory, then incise it and then cure the plague with medicines and restore the flesh to the place of the wound, and command the patient to be sparing of foods in which there is thickness: caps and formed cooked meat and similar to them, until it is composed.
And if there is putrefaction in the wound and it does not adhere to the bone, then you incise all that pus and throw it out, and then cure it.
But if in these plagues an artery or vein is present from which blood can flow, and it is not severed by medicines, then you inquire about the artery, and if you find that not incised, then you incise it with a spatula, or ligate it; and if necessity compels you that what we have said does not agree, then you cauterize until the blood is severed.
And if these plagues are simple and small, then the cause of them is light; so that you pulverize on those this powder, which consolidated before the air changes them.
And the manner of the powder is this: take olive oil, one part, of dragon's blood, two parts, of cauterized earth, three parts; have all three ground and sifted, and of it, fill the plague, and be constricted by a good constriction until it well adheres to it, and be coagulated with the blood.
And then strengthen that with poultices and loosen it, and do not untie it while it is thus that it is not suppurating, for the medicine is not eradicated from it until it is healed.
And some times do this solely cauterize, when you do not have present olive oil and dragon's blood.
And already do this same operation in the great plagues when it is necessary that it be placed on them and be tightened, and are recent plagues with their blood, which the air has not altered.
And if the air has altered them, and especially when it is in summer time, then it is not understood in the position of this powder, but then cure those with what we have said, so that you place on them some digested poultices, or that you place on them powder of barley flour with water and honey until they get pus; and then cure those with the other cure until they are healed.
But if the plague fractures a bone, and it is small, then you extract it with tweezers.
And you will say the cure for skull fractures in that which is poisonous.
Of the plagues of the neck.
But if the plague occurs in the neck, then there is no difference in medication, and between the plague of the head when it is simple.
But if the nerve of the neck is cut or the artery, then if it is the nerve, it is not in its place, but that its cure be avoided with that which makes vehement coagulation, such as zinc and zeger that is vitriol and similar to their nozo to the nerves and contrazo that. And do not place upon the plague any cause of all cold, for the substance of the nerves is cold and the continuation of it is with the brain, which is the most important of all the members.
And if that which is cured by medicines is light, such as it is washed with sweet water, some herbs infused in rose or non-rose oil, and then washed with sweet water and the other pebbles minced in this manner, and humid.
But if the plague is large, then administer suture, or cut the lips of it, and then cure that with powders until it is healed.

Of the plagues of the belly.
The indisposition which happens in the belly is either great, or little, or medium.

And know that the suture of the belly is done in four ways, but two sutures are common that are used in sutures of the other wounds of the body.
And two other sutures proper are used in other wounds, but they are more proper in the suture of the belly.
And I recommend to you each one with exposition and declaration.
Therefore I say that when the wound is small and there is some cause of the hernia through that, and it is difficult to reduce that, then it is done in one of two ways: either by the smallness of the incision as we have said, or when the hernia has come due to the cold of the air.
And therefore when this is so, then you should cleanse that, as you would submerge a sponge or cloth wet in tepid water, or that you have squeezed in water with squill, and cypress, and spikenard, and apply that to the hernia until the inflammation is resolved.
And sometimes do this with wine, which has astringency, and it is better than water alone in the resolution of inflammation.
And therefore, when you see the inflammation resolved, then you moisten the hernia with water in which are boiled elder and mallows, because by this it is alleviated the pain of it with little cause.
But if the pain of it is excused by this cure, then you widen the incision a little with an instrument with which hemorrhoids are incised.

Of the instrument, this is the form of it:
One part of it is sharp, and the other part is not sharp, and the tip is subtle, and not as subtle as a spatula, rather it is blunt a little.

And similarly, if the incision is in one of the two parts of the belly, then you place your attention and your consideration always in this way so that the part in which the wound is is higher than the other.

And this is the common way of suturing: one that you take the needle, or count of needles according to the quantity of the amplitude of the wound; and then lay it from the end of the incision of the ring finger, and tighten the needle one, and another that you do not put thread in the two extremities of the needle, with two extremities of the thread that is below the thread of the parts of the fingers, until you make that penetrate from that part; and you have already added two extremities of the thread and two extremities of the needle, and they are made four orders.
And then tighten with thread double in the circuit of the needle, and sometimes of two parts together, and then add the two lips and the wound by decent addition; and then lay the thickness of the finger and fix another needle in it, and then tie that with thread as you tied with the first needle; and do not cease to do this if there is need with the needles until you have completed the entire constriction of the wound.
And let the needles be medium in thickness and subtlety, because the subtle needles lightly cut the flesh; and the thick ones are difficult to enter in the needle, and therefore for this reason they should be medium in subtlety and thickness.
And do not let the needle be stuck in two extremities of the needle properly too much, so that the flesh is not lightly cut and that the wound is closed before its consolidation.
And do not be prolonged in suturing so that the wound is not prohibited from consolidation.
And then cut the extremities of the needles so that they do not prick the patient in their sleep; and place on the suture puffed powders of every part, which have the extremities of the needles; and leave those until you know that the wound is already consolidated.

But the second sutura is common: and it is that you administer with suturing the four extremities, of the needle and two extremities of the thread, in one go, with a needle in which the thread is enveloped equal in subtlety and thickness.

Of cure of zoster and fistula.
Know that every plague and abscess when it is inflamed and becomes ancient, and is made an ulcer, and is not consolidated and throws out pus all the time and is not cut off, then, in whatever member it may be, universally it is called a fistula and we call that one zoster.
And fistula according to truth is a hardened, white, knot, with which there is no pain and to which the cavity is as the cavity of a bird's bone; and for this reason that one is called by some rizatz, that is, bone.
And it is in some men humid, the one that throws out pus; and very quickly the humidity is cut off in some hours. And some times this humidity is little, and it is thick, and it is subtle.
I have shown all those causes, and their signs, and their cure with medicines in the division.
And I will tell you how to cure a fistula that is made by operation with a knife.
And know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; some of these are fistulas that reach the large veins and arteries, or the nerves, or the head, or the intestine, or the bladder, or any of the ribs, or any of the vertebrae of the spine, or any of the joints composed by composition as if from the hand and foot; and of these, some are located near the main member and resemble it.
And therefore of these fistulas that are this way, those are of the diseases of difficult healing, and do not receive cure, and occupation with it is work and ignorance.
And if it is of the fistulas any the depth of which does not reach these places that have been said, and you wait and confide in the cure of it, and you want to arrive at knowledge of it, then take a probe of iron or of wood, and if the fistula goes straight, and you probe it with it.
But if the fistula is tortuous, then investigate it with a probe of fine lead, because lead with the lightness of its body is eased and curved of its tortuosity.
And if the fistula is having many horrible things, it is not to you possible that you signify on it with a probe.
Therefore, cleanse the orifice by its orifices, because the moisture by which you cleanse it must go to the other orifices and run from them.
And then inquire exquisitely, according to what manner it is possible for you to know if here has the bone or the nerve, and if the concavity of the fistula is distant or proximate, or if it is a fistula which has many orifices and is above all with the sum of your strength, with your interrogation, with which you interrogate the patient, and the invention of the pain you owe your compression with the hand over the place, and resemblances of the significations and of the causes accidental to the abscess.

Of the cure of the bowels and the quality of clysters with medicines.
When an abscess occurs in certain fleshy members and the space of the abscess is prolonged until it makes a collection of pus, and then it is broken and perforated, and pus is extracted from it, and the place remains empty like it was a vessel, and the skin that is above it as subtle as cloth, and no further corruption has reached it, and it does not imprint on the bone or on the nerves or on the ligaments, it is called a sinus, and it is not called a fistula.
But however, if the space is prolonged until the corruption imprints on some member, then it is called a fistula and not a sinus.
And the cure of it is that the skin is incised completely as it is revolved, and mostly when it is subtle and is made like cloth, and composes that it does not adhere to the place by its corruption.
But if you hope that the skin adheres and that that corruption has not achieved further consequence, and in the skin has passed through a face, then you cure that with clysters.
And it is that you consider the sinus, and then if it is large, and the brac that you see is of fetid odor, then you clysterize that with an Egyptian medicine which is of oil and wine and vinegar, receiving equal parts, and they are adjusted in a vessel, and they are cooked over the fire until the medicine becomes thick and reaches the consistency of honey.
And then you take from it what is necessary and dissolve it in water and honey; and clysterize with that the sinus, and strengthen the orifice of it, and leave the medicine in it for the quantity of two hours.
And then extract that with a sponge; and do this for so many days until the sinus is purified and the stench is removed.
And some times it is clysterized with ash water, when this medicine is not present to you; and it is that you take the ash of beech, and put on it water; and then collect that and clysterize with it until you confess that the sinus is then stayed.
And if the patient does not tolerate the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water, then clysterize that with water and honey and that it is mixed with vinegar, and clysterize that with wine and honey mixed, because of the property of honey is that it purifies and washes, and the wine makes the sinus adhere, and especially when in the wine there is superfluity of astringency and dryness.
And as you do this sometimes and you confess that the sinus is already removed, then clysterize that with water that makes flesh grow in it.

Of the cure of panaritia and ingrown toenails and the addition of finger incision and section.
Panaritia is an abscess which nails from the nail of the finger or of the foot, and often nails in the other fingers, and as it is prolonged and its cure is less valued, or is an abscess of abscess caut, or is corrupted, and throws out arm until it corrodes the roots of the nail, and often corrupts that whole, and often it spreads its corruption to the bone until it is to it a fetid odor, and is made the extremity of the finger lamed, and the color of it is made dusky.
And therefore when you will have that with the water that we have said in the division and do not apply your cure, then cove that you cut with iron all the superfluity that is remained of the nail and then cauterize the wound with water, because cauterization much is useful in that.
But if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy, and the additions of the nail voids already comprehend the flesh to the parts of the finger, and begin to pierce it and to let out that, then cove that you pause a fine ray below the angle of the nail that pierces the flesh, and impel that up and cut that flesh with facility, and place on that which remains of the flesh of the medicines corrosive comburent until it be all removed; and then cure that with poultices until it be healed.
But if the corruption has already entered the bone, then cove that you cut the bone that and extract it, for no time is healed that there is in it the corrupted bone.
And if you see the corrosion and corruption going into the wound, then you should cut it in one of the nuts according to how it is pressed, and then take care of it until it is healed.
If the nail is damaged by a blow or friction, and there is intense pain in that area, then when you first begin to treat the patient, you should carefully cut the nail with a sharp spatula, making a transverse cut from top to bottom, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh that remains under the nail, because you will cause the patient intense pain and lead to the formation of excess fleshy tissue in the area; and then treat the area with water that soothes the pain.
But this adjusted flesh, which is born in the hands of some men, is very fleshy, and it is very much in their bones, or very much in their nails.
And some of them are born at the base of the joint, or the birth of them in some of the nuts of the hands. But the one that is born in some of the nuts of the finger does not get worse, and this one that is born in the joints is very much worse.
And of those that are born fleshy, the incision is lighter, and it is that you should cut that with the root of the spatula.
But of the one that is born at the base of the joint, the cure is difficult; and therefore, beware of the abscess of it.
But in the one that is born in the finger, you should cut the flesh of it at the beginning with a round incision into the bone, and then saw with one of those saws convenient to water, and then take care of it until it is healed.
But consolidation, which happens to the fingers between their movements or by birth of the man who is born that way, or by consolidation of plague or by burning of fire, or by similar things, therefore, you should cut that consolidation so that the fingers return to their natural form.

Of incisions of vices, they are varicose.
