Chapter XIV.
Of the restoration of the fracture of the bone of the hip.
The bone of the hip many times is broken and is declared to the sentiment according to that it is converted to the part in front and to the most sovereign.
And the restoration of it is made as if the ligament is strengthened over the fracture and another ligament below the fracture, and the patient be prostrate upon his belly and upon the face.
And then the minister extends the entire ligament to its part according to the quality, when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
But if it is proper to the root of the thigh, then the ligament is properly attached to the bone at the part of the pelvis, so that the extension is placed on it, and the other ligament is left at the fracture.
And similarly, if the fracture is proper to the bone, then the ligament is made proper to the bone, and the extension is to the parts below.
And then the doctor aligns the bones with both his hands while reducing it according to the natural resemblance and the bone is joined by a good connection; then, cover it with plaster and a splint, if it does not happen to the limb abscess. But if it happens to it abscess, then you leave it for some days until the abscess has cauterized, and then return to your cure.
The splint of it is made like this: cover over the fracture a hard bandage, and double it two or three times, and remove from it the superfluity; and then encase the leg until it reaches the hip and the root of the thigh.
And introduce a long stick between the thigh and the leg, from the bone to the parts below, and the ends of the stick from the sovereign part of both parts, and then roll over the leg and thigh what superfluity of the bandage.
And then place on the thigh in the place of that fracture splints, and place from those one splint on the bone of the leg.
And then fill the vacancies between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths, so that the splint is coagulated.
And then begin with a strong splint of the middle over the place of the fracture with three or four wrappings, and as much as you go away with the ligament from the place of the fracture, your splint is less and lighter and softer.
And then extend both ends of the stick to the parts below until it reaches the heel of the foot, and strengthen both ends of the splints on the other side so that the ligament is not removed from its place.
And then leave the splint on it, so that it does not happen to the limb corrosion or cauterized abscess or inflammation and similar to those; and if it happens any cause of those, then cut yourself from it, and rectify what happens to it all again, according to what we have said many times.
But if in the bone is a piece of bone that puts, then cover that according to what is possible to you; and if not, then finish on it and remove that, and cure with what preceded the memory until it is healed.
And sometimes this fracture of the thigh is strengthened with another thing that are adjusted to it splints, as we have said in the adjutant and in the arm.
But however in the restoration of it in such a manner made do not happen to the patient lameness; and if it is restored alone, then another thing that is applied to the other leg, then it is necessary that he limp from the one that is always.
And know that the thigh is strengthened in 40 days or a few more or a few less, and all that is according to the diversity of the complexities and of the other dispositions.
Chapter XV.
Of the restoration of the fracture of the kneecap of the bone.
Know that a fracture of the kneecap of the bone takes time, but it happens to it many times attrition.
But if it happens to it fracture, then it is not but a fissure or crack in its parts, and that is with a plaguer or several plaguers, and over that all is placed with the sentiment.
And the restoration of it is in such a way that it is aligned what is broken of its parts with the saids until it is joined and conjoined according to what is possible by equation and facility and fabrication.
And then place plaster and place on it a round splint, if you need it; and strengthen above it with a splint to what is convenient.
And then consider all the dispositions which we have recommended in the other fractures, as well as cauterized abscess and similar to those in such a way that it opposes all accidents to what is convenient to it until it is healed.
Chapter XVI.
Of the restoration of the fracture of the leg.
Know that in the leg there are two bones of which one is thick, and it is called by the name of the leg; and the other is subtle, and it is called fibula.
And it happens to some of the species of fracture that happens to the two bones of the leg, and for that reason is made restoration of it as well as restoration of the arm aligned, and the operation of it is one.
And if the two bones are broken together, the leg is converted to all parts.
And if the more subtle bone is broken, the leg is converted to the parts before.
And if the thicker bone is broken, it is turned below, and it is of those causes that are not to your liking.
And then administer extension, flexion, and ligation of the bones according to that alignment.
But however, if the fracture of the leg is light and has few splints, that the extension be less and more gently, and alleviate with your virtue.
And in the leg there is some cause for operation on the arm, and it is when you align the bones and that completes all your operation, then you will take pieces of wood of pine which is placed under the causes which are placed in soles, and they are made of palm branches; some of those to which is small thickness, and not be of the handles, and be the length of those according to the length of the leg, and from the knee to the foot.
And then envelope on each side in two envelopes according to their length, and place one on the side of the leg on one side and the other on the other side, and be from the knee to the foot.
And then tie the two bones in three places of two extremities and in the middle place, for with this structure the leg is prohibited from bending to the right and left side, and it stands for good station.
And now is administered a splint of wood according to the length of the leg; and be placed in it the leg so that it conserve that of movement.
And mostly, that you do this in a fracture, and when with that is plague properly.
And then consider in each day the leg and study with that by behind study, and you guard it from abscess and from inflammation or other causes similar; and when it happens some cause of those, then oppose yourself to it with that which must be done until it be healed.
Chapter XVII.
Of the fracture of the heel and of the bones of the foot and of the digits.
To the heel, fractures do not happen often; but to the bones of the foot, fractures happen sometimes; and to the digits of the foot, few fractures happen, and they do not happen to them but attrition in the middle of the disposition.
And if to the bones of the foot, a fracture happens and sometimes those bones be elevated above themselves among them, then the patient places his foot on the ground prepared as if walking.
And then place the one foot on that which is elevated of those bones, and then step on them, and press, and align them until they return to their places.
And then place plaster and stoppings above, and place below the belly of the foot a small table to which are two plastic heads.
And then strengthen that with the foot in structure descent, because you have enveloped that with cloths and other causes of which you have indicated.
And when three days or four have passed, then you untie the ligament, because you have found the bones aligned, or be fractured or be dislocated, and the operation in those is so as you know.
But if some digits are fractured, then restore those, and align them as I have told you in the restoration of the digits of the hand. And then place on the fractured digit a splint according to the length of the digit, and be a little wider than it; and below the foot this table which I have told you, and strengthen that with stricture decent.
But if that which is fractured of the bones are two or three or more, then you place on each digit a splint of its quantity enveloped in linen cloth, and strengthen the table in the lowest part of the foot, and be standing on one of the heads of the table the belly of the foot so that it has with good retention.
And it is convenient to you that you do not forget that you do not consider all the causes which you have been told to you in the other fractures of the accidents that we have said; and oppose yourself to every accident with that which must be done.
Chapter XVIII.
Of the fracture of the hip of the woman and of the bone of the thigh and of the groin of the man.
When the hip of the woman is fractured, then make that cease in a cradle fallen, and then incline that to the side of the back a little, and be held behind.
And then the matron impales the hip with a cloth, and be made in the hip of her as you hope; and then the woman be moved, and elevate the back of her little by little, because all that is cast out until it be in front of the hip as you hope and the fractured bone returns.
And then place powders on the back of her, and when she wants to urinate, remove the cloth with facility and then urine, and reduce and return that according to the manner according to which you have seen that at the beginning, and then return to her first powder.
And do so for seven days or around those, because that is restored.
And if you want, take a bladder of sheep and strengthen over the back of her a tube of cane; and introduce the whole bladder into the hip of her, and then insufflate into the tube with virtue until the bladder be inflated within the hip, because the fracture returns.
And then be filled with cloth and stay for some days according to which we have recommended, until it be healed.
And when the bones of the thigh of a man or a woman are broken, then administer in the restoration and stitching of it that which we have recounted in the bone of the hip.
And that which is straight is not hidden in these proper fractures and which few understand, mostly to him who has some study and use and understands this my book well; for that fracture signifies to you in the major dispositions the straight way in the restoration and the stricture of it, and therefore understand well.
But in the leg of a man when it is broken, take a splint of wood, and put the leg in it; and then place on it a wrapping of cloth, and it be wrapped, and then be left for three days or thereabouts, and it be healed.
Chapter XIX.
Of the restoration of fractures of bones when it is accompanied by plague.
It is convenient for him to whom a fracture occurs with plague, and especially if the bone is large as is the bone of the thigh or of the arm, or similar to that, that you take care and flebotomize it as soon as the conditions of flebotomy to you or testify as we have said above.
And if the plague flows blood, then you must take care to its retention as much as you pulverize over it  zegi trissat, if to you another cause is not present.
And then as you begin to restore the fracture in that same day, and do not prolong it, if you do not occur an abscess.
But if an abscess occurs, then you leave the restoration of it until the ninth day, until it is yielded the abscess, and do not approach it in the third day and the fourth of all, for you will cause to occur bad accidents.
But if the broken bone is eminent upon the uncovered condyle, then you must take care to perforate to reduce it and stitch it with your hands with facility and with little extension.
But if extension is not to you prepared and the equation of it with your hands, then you reduce it with your hands with this instrument; and it is the instrument which is made of iron, the length of which is of seven digits or of eight and the width of which is according to the quantity of the plague; and for that it is necessary to the physician that he prepare of those three or four according to the quantity that you indiges ad that in the cure in all species of fracture.
And let it be round, and let it have in it little thickness so that it not be bent of necessity the comprehension upon it in the hour of the operation.
And let it be of acute extremity to which let be margin in its extremities; and let the underside of it to be of tending thickness, and of the majority of it within to the parts.
And this is the form of it:
And it is named in Greek "labre volentz atelarem", so it is a little palette.
For that it must be placed the extremity of it attends elevated upon the extremity of the bone eminent.
And impel it in a single stroke while it returns the bone, and it be stitched with some equation.
And therefore strive you to stitch the extremities of the fracture between them, and if the extremity of it broken is subtle, and does not take that the instrument for good acceptance, then you must insert the extremity of that bone while the instrument has power of it.
But if you cannot reduce the bone of all with that which we have recounted, then inscise it with that which convenes to it of the incisors which we have said; or saw it with one of the saws in whatever manner be to you possible.
And then ratze those which remain in the bone of asperity and of small scales.
And as the bone is reduced, and then the reduction the patient suffers vehement pain, then you know that the bone is not returned to its natural place; and therefore do that which you confer to the patient great help.
When is completed your restoration which you do to the bone, and then submerge cloth in vi stiptic black, and properly if it is in summer, and do not place upon the plague cerot nor other cause in which there be oil, so that it not do in it occur pox and corruption.
And then administer stelas in the hour of your compliment of the restoration of the bone, and leave the plague uncovered as much as you inscise the tract with forceps and uses of bandages according to the quantity of the plague.
And guard yourself with all caution that you do not strain the plague with the fracture, for many times have done this the foolish physicians, and have caused to occur upon their patients death or disease corrupting or ulcerating, so it is healed. And if your stitching is lighter, soft, different from the stitching of other fractures.
And if the plague is great or is a bad plague, and you fear upon that some bad accidents which we have recounted, and you suffer pain in the place, then you must not place upon it stelas, but do to it an enveloping of hard cloths in place of stelas and strain it with those.
And when about a day or two already the plague begins, that in it be engendered brac, then you oust from below the cloth which you had placed upon it with vi, and then administer calques, unguents with which of our custom is that we medicate the plagues, as well as unguents tetrafarmacon and similar to that.
And it is necessary for you to untie the ligament and consider the plague on each day morning and evening until it is consolidated and fixed, and so that the limb is prepared in such a manner that the pus runs from it to the parts below with ease.
If many days pass to the plague, and it is not consolidated nor is it separated from it the limb, then you know that here are satagias of the small ones for which you should inquire the plague with care. And of those satagias those that are separated remove and extract, those that from them are not separated and put the limb and cause to occur pain, pierce to you to incise those according to what to you is possible.
And if it happens to the plague to become slimy or to ooze, it is a sign of a corruption and of putrefaction, then you should apply to each of those with the water that is necessary to them of the cure of which is preceded narration in its chapter.
And of this in which you should know the best way and you make present your person: when the bone is broken, set it upon the limb as the bone of the thigh and of the helper and similar to those of the large limbs, and that you do not presume to traction of it, nor the extraction of it for many times it happens by this death; have left it within that you are able, for very soon it will fall by itself in about twenty days or thirty; And then cure the plague if to you is seen, and if not leave that.
Chapter XX.
Of the cure of nodules that happen in the vestigi of any fracture.
Many times it happens this nodule in the vestigi of the healing of a fracture, and mostly that it is near the joints, and it is ornamented by it the figure of the limb; and very soon it prohibits the limb from its natural operation.
Therefore consider if the nodule is recent and administer in that medicines that have stipulated as such as aloes, and incense, and mira, and cercacollo, and acridity, and similar to those; in this way that you take of that some or all, and confit those with vi stiptic, or with album of hen, or with vi agre, and place that upon the nodule in cotton, and constrict those upon it for good constriction.
And leave the constriction that you do not untie that for many days; and about untie that and iterate another, within that it is removed the nodule; or strengthen upon that lamina of lead descentment, for lead has property of removing all that is inflated in the limbs.
But if nodule already is in a worse converted and tight is and necessity provokes to ostracize that coitadament, and then cut that by the part sovereign of it, and incise that the superfluity and eminent, or rat that with some rezoris within that it is removed; and cure that within that it is healed.
Chapter XXI.
Of restoration of fracture when it is restored and about that remains the limb subtle and frail not according to its nature.
When fracture of bone is restored, and about that remains the limb subtle and frail, then that is not done but for many causes: of which one is multitude of solution of the ligament and of the ligation of it made not according to what is necessary; or for superfluity of constriction of the ligaments within that the nourishment is prohibited to run to the limb; or for multitude of superfluous embrocation; or for superfluous movement not in its hour; or for paucity of blood in the body of the patient and for weakness of it.
And cure of that is to give to the patient to eat and make the heart of him tender within that the blood is multiplied in him; and administer baths; and introduce joy and happiness upon him.
And about place poultice upon the limb, so that the poultice draws to it much nourishment, or continues embrocation of it with water tebeza, within that the nourishment runs and returns to its natural figure.
Chapter XXII.
Of cure of the bones broken when they are restored tortuously and prohibits the operation of them of that which is necessary.
When it happens to the limb already restored about the healing of it from tortuosity and eminence to the broken bone and nodule, and it is for that feeded of form of the limb, but however the limb is not prohibited of its natural operation, then you should not receive the word of that one who exists that member be of new broken.
But already are stood many foolish physicians and restorers the ones who have done that in our land; and this operation is very vituperable, perdoing a great fear the sign of which is mortal.
But if claudication and nodule are recent, then you should be embrocated with water tebeza in which are cotas mollificant herbs, such as are  roots of altea and roots of it, and melilot, and similar to those; and be made a poultice with mollifying poultice as diallaquilon well made; or that be prized mucillage of root of altea and be contused with gray of guanine or with oil of ceram, and be emplastered with that; or that be prized figs fatty and be trissated with fems of pigeon, and similar to those of the medicines that are called amermans consolidation.
And some times it is dissolved with assiduous friction lighter that be with the hands humid, and be administered movement of the limb to all part in all hours.
But if the curvature has already been added and is strong and converted into a worse state and the need for its cure arises with iron, then it is necessary that the pus be above the abscess and the continuity of the bone be dissolved, and it is incised that which is superfluous of the knot of that part with the bone with subtle scissors, and is administered facility in that with solicitude and study.
Chapter XXIII.
On the speech of dislocation.
Dislocation is the displacement of any of the joints of the body, so that movement is prohibited, and the shape of the limb is altered, causing great pain and injury to the patient.
Therefore, when a dislocation occurs, it is necessary to immediately attempt to reduce it, and not delay that reduction, because if it is delayed, the place becomes inflamed and very difficult to reduce the dislocation.
And for this, one should not be negligent or stretched out during the time of inflammation, because often it brings on spasms and intense pains.
But when this happens, then it is necessary to cut the patient's clothing and allow the inflammation to rest; and then the limb should be enveloped with warm water and oil, and then it should be reduced with ease.
And every member should be treated with that which will bring remembrance to its place.
And now, I have ordered the chapters on dislocation according to what has been previously said about fractures; from the part of the body that is more sovereign to the part that is less.
Chapter XXIV.
On the cure of dislocation of the lower jaw.
So the two jaws are dislocated if not treated; and the dislocation of both is made in one of two ways: either they are slightly moved from their places and softened a little; or they are dislocated completely and complicatedly, so that they are softened at the joint where the saliva of the patient flows and that it cannot hold or close its mouth, and the tongue of it is enveloped in its word.
But when the dislocation of it is slight, then in the major dispositions it returns by itself with little cause.
But if the dislocation is complete and complicated, then it is necessary to administer its reduction gently, and not delay it at all.
And it is that the minister has the head of the patient, and the physician inserts the tip of his finger into the root of the dislocation of the lower jaw from inside his mouth, if the dislocation is on one side; or that he inserts both of his fingers together, if the dislocation is on both sides, and the other said ones of his are outside with which he enguals; and commands the patient to cease his jaws and release those to go from any part; and the physician enguals the jaw and pushes the jaw until it returns to its place.
And if the reduction is difficult, and especially if both jaws are dislocated at the same time, then administer evaporation with warm water and oil, until the reduction of both is made easier and do not delay the reduction of both at all, as we have said.
And therefore, when they return and are engualed, and the mouth of the patient is closed and not softened, then place on them powders of cloth with cerot, and make it of wax and oil rubbed; and then it is applied with ease with soft bandages.
And let the patient sleep on his back, and his head be standing between two pillows, so that he does not hurt either to the right or to the left; and do not force him to chew anything; having his food be forbidden lion, until when the pains are softened and the jaws are numbed, then allow him to chew as he wants.
And that be administered with ease, and do not work on the opening of the mouth of the patient, the eating and drinking and spitting, until the jaw is numbed and healed.
And if the reduction of two jaws when dislocated in any hour and not converted to their places is difficult, then often this happens fever and continuous soda, and very much is alarmed the belly of the patient, and very much and vomits pure cholera.
And when you see this, then you know that it is perilous; and often many die to whom this happens in x days.
Chapter XXV.
On the reduction of the dislocation of the clavicle and of the extremity of the muscle.
The clavicle is not dislocated from the place between the feet by its continuity with the feet; and sometimes it is dislocated at the outer part, and this is declared to the touch.
And the restoration of it is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms. And then grasp the place with your palm with great force, so that it will return.
And then place on it an ointment and powders and strengthen that.
But the extremity of that which is tied and continued with it, is not dislocated in any day; then it is necessary to be reduced and engualed according to what we have said and according to what is your apparatus.
And then place on it an ointment, and powders, and an extrication, and command the patient to adhere to tranquility and rest until it is healed.
And in this same treatment, the extremity of the muscle is reduced when it is separated from its place.
Chapter .xxvi.
Of the reduction of the dislocation of the muscle.
Know that the muscle is not dislocated except in three ways, of which one is that it is dislocated from the part of the thigh to the part below.
And the second is that it is dislocated at the part below the muscle, and that is done hard; and it is not dislocated at the parts behind by the shoulder; and it is not dislocated at the parts in front by the nerves.
And mostly it is dislocated and exits outside at the parts below the thigh, and mostly in those whose flesh is little, it is easily dislocated; but in those in which there is much flesh, it is exited outside with difficulty.
And often it happens to some men by percussion or fall, and the muscle of him is apoplected by apoplexy, and it is cured by that which is already dislocated.
Therefore, it is necessary that you know this before you are over-certain of him, and then proceed in the cure of him.
And it is known the dislocation of him when it is at the parts below the thigh; so that you distinguish between the dislocated muscle and the healthy muscle, because you find between those a manifest diversity; and you find in the head of the muscle concavity and below the thigh of the touch of the head of the muscle as if a hollow, and the patient cannot reduce his hand to his armpit, nor move that by all movements.
If it is dislocated below the foot or above, and you then find a manifest touch, and it is not hidden.
And of this dislocation is made light reduction when it is fresh and the patient is young.
And the reduction of him is that the minister elevates the hand of him to the parts above; and then places his feet below the thigh of him, and elevates the joint with strength upwards to its place, and the minister elevates the hand of him, and extends that upwards; and then places that below as it returns slightly.
But if by what we have said it does not return, and it is from the beginning that the dislocation happened, many days, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in warm water and be administered a broth that softens and lubricates as if it were cooked with roots of altea, fennel, and melilot in water, and be administered.
And then the patient be laid on his back and be placed below the thigh of him, waiting for a wool that be equal between levitated and stricture, and then the physician places his hand over the sphere, and elevates the head of the muscle with virtue, and pulls the hand of the patient so that it not be moved to the parts below, and another minister holds the head of the patient, so that it not be moved to the parts below, for that at once returns to its place.
And if you want, reduce it this way: and it is that you make a man present who is longer than the patient, and he is on the part of that side, and interweaves his muscle below the thigh of the patient and elevates his thigh to the parts above while the patient is suspended in air, and another minister pulls the hand of the patient from the parts below his belly. But if the patient is light, then it is necessary that with him that another cause be suspended, so that it weighs that one, for the dislocation returns at once.
And it is reduced easily in another way: and it is that on the ground be placed a long pole the head of which be round in figure, as if a mortar, that it not be thick nor thin, and then it be placed below the patient; because being placed on the head of the pole cloths lions, and the patient be standing according to the length of the pole, and then be extended the hand of him to the parts below the other part; and be extended the body of him from the other part with strength, for the joint returns to its place with speed.
And if it is difficult reduction of him for all the causes that we have said, then use of this cure: and it is that you take a pole the quantity of which be in the length of two arms, and latitude of that be of four digits, and the thickness of it be alleviated in the preon of the thigh according to this form:
And then on the round head be laid cloths lions so that the pole does not injure the patient.
And then it be placed below the thigh of the patient, and be extended the hand or arm over the pole into the parts below, and be tied the pole over the assistant and the arm and the extremity of the hand.
Then be placed the arm on a step of a ladder according to the latitude, and the hand be extended to the parts below, and the other body be suspended from the other part, for the joint enters at once.
And as the entry of him is completed according to whichever manner that is possible to you, then it is necessary that you place below the thigh a sphere of wool of equal quantity; and then place plaster prepared of powder of meal with eggs and album of hen over the whole muscle, as if it were rolled upwards, and then strengthen below the thigh with decent stricture; and the ligament be rolled over the plaster, and the hand of him be attached to the neck of him, and be left, and not be moved the hand of him for seven days.
And that the patient's food be kept meager, until the limb is comforted, for it is lighter to the healing of it.
And then the food should be given more, near wine or vinegar, and exercise is made; and therefore if it is stopped and not softened, then it is already healed.
But if the joint is dislocated many times by humidity that happens to it or by another cause, then it should be administered cauterization with three furrows, according to what was said before in the chapter of cauterization.
And if all this is done and after seven days the ligament is loosened and the joint is not fixed, and the plaster and strapping are reduced over it several times, and it is not fixed and catz and cannot raise that arm to the upper parts, then know that the nerves of it, which are at the head of the muscle, are already severed or stretched or softened, and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Of the dislocation of which is made of the foot and the heel or the parts behind, the reduction is made with impulse and extension with the hands, until it returns.
And let the other strapping be administered there, and cure that until it is healed.
And if it happens that near the healing gravity settles in the limb and slowness in the movement of it, then the patient uses baths many times until that gravity is alleviated and that it returns to its first nature.
Chapter .xxvii.
Of the cure of dislocation of the hip.
Know that the hip joint is dislocated with difficulty and seems to return with difficulty; and it is dislocated to all parts, and mostly to the front part to the back part, and the dislocation of it is not easily guessed because it is hidden by the skin or by the touch according to which figure it is dislocated, and when you adjust the dislocated hip with the hand, this is clearly declared to you, because the joint is concave and cannot bend the arm, nor touch with that its muscle.
And that you, with your hands, reduce the dislocation as soon as possible before an abscess comes to it, because if an abscess comes to it, the reduction is difficult, and it is not healed entirely; and especially when it is to the back parts, because it is the worst of all kinds of dislocations, and of greater pain, and many times they die from it.
And the restoration of it, when it is possible to reduce it, is that the hand of it be extended with two hands, and the arm of it be expanded, and the hands of the doctor be upon the hip and below it, and he pushes the joint with the knuckles of his hands at the same time, or with the root of his palm until it returns to its place.
But if the dislocation is to the front parts, then it returns so that he bends his hand with his hand, until he strikes the hip with the root of his palm.
And if the dislocation does not obey the reduction, then administer vehement extension and strong force.
And it is that two ministers extend the arm, and hold that raising of the ministers so that it is not removed from the extension.
And then it be revolved the arm completely, because it is enveloped with a long folded cloth over the hand of it, or ligament.
And when the doctor touches the joint with his hand, anoint it with some oil so that this is those causes which help in the lubrication of the joint with ease; and then push the joint with a vehement impulse until it returns.
And after the reduction of it, it should be laid upon that plaster in which there is a stich and a covering with album of egg, and it is extended with a descending strapping, and the arm be suspended from the neck, and be left for several days.
And after it is loosened; and then if the joint is formed in its place, then you untie the strapping of it and leave it.
And if sometimes the joint does not become stronger, then you repeat the plaster and the strapping, and leave it for several days until it is extended; and then untie it.
But if it happens to it gravity after the reduction of the joint, and the disposition of it is in movement, then administer moisture in baths and subtle friction, and compression, until it is alleviated; or pause upon the joint alleviated, so it is a soft cloth; and then be tied, and leave it upon the bones day and night. And after that, put that in a bath; and when it dries, then you rub the joint with temperate friction, and then repeat upon it the alleviated, so it is a soft cloth, once, and the second, and the third. Corruption has already arrived on the enamel inside the bath, while it is lined.
And if you wish, place upon it a piece of wet cowhide scraped with a knife and stretched over it; and do this several times, because it is moist and reduces it to its disposition.
Chapter .xxviii.
Of the cure of dislocation of the malassen, so it is of the joint that is between the arm and the hand.
Malassen of the hand some times is dislocated, and the reduction of the dislocation of it is lighter, and the contrary is of the other joints, but however, that it should be velocity in the reduction of it in the hour in which it is dislocated, before the place be apostemat or that something happens to it abscess.
And the reduction of the dislocation of him is that you place the joint of the patient's arm on a table and the minister extends the arm of that, and the doctor places his hand or his palm on the prominence of the joint, and pushes it until it returns to its place.
But however, it must be considered if the palm is already placed in the belly of the arm, then the patient places the back of his arm on a table, both extension and reduction; and if the dislocation is anterior, then the position of the arm of that one intrinsically on the table, so that the hand of the doctor is placed on that prominence of the joint.
And therefore if it returns immediately, it is good; and if not, then strengthen that with a poultice, yielding the abscess and leaving it; and do not repeat this, because if not, do not suffer nor can you on the reduction of it more than days pass.
But however, the joint remains according to its tortuosity; and do not notice to the patient any cause, except that the arm is softened and cannot strengthen any cause; then you know that the nerves are cut or torn, and then there is no way but that it be strengthened with a cautery near the place of it and for a long time confer any cause.
Therefore, when the bad arm is returned, then place on it the poultice which you have recomposed, and let it be left and strengthened for five days; and then it is removed and let it be left and the arm of it be exercised.
But if the movement of it is stayed and there is any gravity in it, then gently that with water cauda and with friction some times, until it is alleviated.
Chapter XXIX.
Of the cure of dislocations of the said.
Sometimes the fingers are dislocated in every part.
And when a finger is dislocated of those to the back of the palm or to the belly of it, then stretch the finger and push the dislocation of it with your thumbs, until it returns.
And then support the head of the finger, and suspend that with the part to which it is dislocated, and leave it for two days.
And then suspend that and extend that until straight it be equal in that day.
And when it will be night, lie that according to that narration, and do not cease to untie that in the day and exercise with movement, and lie that in the night; and do this for some days until it be straight.
And do similar with this, if it is dislocated to the belly of the arm, and lie that to that part and do with this your first operation, until it be healed.
And similarly do with this when it is dislocated to the other parts.
Chapter XXX.
Of the cure of dislocations of the vertebrae of the back.
When there occurs to any of the vertebrae of the back or of the neck a dislocation complicated, and are removed moved vertebrae from their places, then in that there is no cure, because death seizes the patient.
And a sign of this is that the digestion of the patient is outside his will, and cannot retain that; and many times are softened some members of him or both legs of him or two arms of him, or one of those; or is removed a vertebra from its place, because many times is removed and many times is made the removal of those to four parts.
Therefore that already is removed to the parts behind and is named gelbozzitat.
But the cure of it is that then you consider if the gelbozzitat occurs from puerility, because then in that there is no cure nor of that there is no healing of all.
But in that which comes from a wound or from percussion or similar to those, already said the Ancients the ways of cure with sermo prolixs, of which the most returns with prophecy; but I have already and abbreviated of that of which the little excuse of the excess of it, for my better proximity to my better understanding exposition, with which I have this exposed and formed ex instrument divers of that with which I will show this and expose that.
And of those there is no cured except that which occurs in the back properly with what I have recomposed.
And it is that the patient be extended on his face on a bed near a wall, and be extended below him a soft instrument so that the feet of him not be lifted.
And then a straight stick be placed, fixed in the ground at the extremity of the bed around the head of it, and another stick in the air the feet of it at the other extremity of the bed.
And the minister hold the stick, and not be stopped in fossa; and another minister hold the other according to that form.
And then envelope over the head of the patient and below the little limbs leon firm; and extend the extremity of the limb to the stick which is above the head of it, and lie that in it; and then strengthen the other limb over the hips of it the denols of it, and below the legs of it; and then adjust all the limbs and lie those in the other stick which is above the feet of it.
And then the minister, with a cascu, extends the ligament to the part of the shaft, and do not be removed the two shafts and ligaments of their places in which they are placed, but however, do not be fixed as we have said.
And the doctor places his palms on the spine with strength while it returns, or that which places upon it a table, and then adjusts upon the table his feet while it returns.
But if it does not return in this way, then take a table of which the width or length is in average of three arms, and carve in the side of which we have said that is near the patient a place in which enters the extremity of the table. And then place the majority of the table upon the spine, and the doctor places his feet upon the other extremity, and tightens well until the spine is shortened and returns to its place.
And if you want, open with a turn the one which is revolved with the hand; and it is that you fix in the ground the head of the patient in the rear of the pug two shafts, the length of which is of an arm, and in the rear of the pug also two shafts; and let the length that is between each shaft be a palm, and already is made in each shaft a hole in which runs the turn, and each one be fixed in the ground so that it is not moved.
And let it be also a shaft round in which is the turn, and let it be revolved in the two holes of the two shafts.
And in the extremity of it is a hole in which is formed the shaft, the length of which is a palm with that which is revolved; and in the two other shafts is similar to that.
And then tighten the ligaments that you have straightened in the feet of the patient in the hole which is opposite the head of it, and the ligaments that you have straightened in the thighs of it in the turn which is opposite the feet of it.
And then opposite each turn and there be a minister that twists the turn with his hand, and the doctor aligns the spine according to what we have said.
And as soon as the spine is returned, and the place is aligned, then cover with a plaster drying with album of egg, and then with cotton; and then place upon the plaster a board of the table of which the width is three fingers or about those, and the length of it is the quantity that engulfs the place of the belly, and upon the part of the spine.
And then tie it with the ligament which we have said, and use the patient of subtle nourishment while it is healing.
And if there remain any prominence in the place at the end of the healing, then it is necessary that medicines be administered which soften and lubricate with administration of the table for a long time, which we have recommended; and already is administered in that place a sheet of lead.
And some times accidents happen prominence in the rear of the spines of the two, and it is cured by that dislocation; and it is that bone which already protrude because it is not necessary that it be done a prognosis to it with this medicine, because very strong it will make you happen death.
Chapter .XXXI.
Of the cure of a dislocated hip.
Know that the joint of the hip and the joint of the muscle should not be dislocated only, and accidents happen to those that happen to the other joints of small movement and concavity.
And the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four ways, because it is dislocated to the front parts, or to the back parts, or to the front parts, or to the back parts.
And most of all it is dislocated to the front parts, and few to the front parts or to the back parts.
And the sign of the dislocation of it to the front parts is that, when you adjust the leg of the healthy patient with the patient, it is longer and the thigh is more prominent than of the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend his foot opposite the leg, and it is the place that if the leg is apostate of pus caut, so that the head of the thigh has already arrived here.
And the sign of that one which happens dislocation is to the back parts, is that the accidents of it are contrary to this accident.
And the sign of that one which happens dislocation to the front parts is that it expands its leg according to its completion, but however it does not bend that it hurts in the thigh, and if it tries to go and cannot upon that to the front parts; and the urine of it is retained and the groin of it is apostate, and because of the ambulation of it upon the talus.
And the sign of that one which happens dislocation to the back parts is that it does not expand the thigh, nor can it bend that in front that it bends the groin, and the leg of it is shorter than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the thigh is opposite that place.
But the reduction of the species of this dislocation is that you consider, then, if the dislocation is old and antique, that it is already fixed with that having it, then you administer reduction of it and remains according to its disposition, then it is not in that cure of all; and therefore it is not necessary that in that one be done a prognosis.
But in the case of a recent dislocation, and it is one of the four species of dislocation, then take hold of it so that you turn the joint and extend it to the inner and outer parts, and move it to the right and left, for it will return strongly and does not need other treatment.
But if it does not return in this manner, then take hold of it so that you prepare a strong minister and extend the leg of him from the farthest part, or by his hands, or by a bandage which is tied over the leg below the knee; and another minister extends the hand of him from below so that it places his hands below the heels of him; and then tighten with a bandage on the root of the thigh, and hold another minister the extremity of the bandage.
And its extension from him or from the inner part to the shoulder or from the back to the part of the loins.
And the extension of all those at once while the patient is elevated with his body from the ground and remains hanging.
And this species of extension is common to all four.
And therefore if the dislocation returns with what we have said, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary for all species to do what I will say of the proper cure.
In the reduction of the own, when it is dislocated, and the dislocation is in the inner parts, then the patient should be laid down on his side; and then place the bandages on the root of the thigh in that place which is between the head of the thigh and the place that is below the shoulder; and then extend the bandage from the part of the shoulder to the highest part of the clavicle.
And then another minister strongly presses the arms of him, and grasps the thick part of the thigh of the patient and extends to the outer parts by vehement extension, for that returns to its place.
And this species is of the lightest cure with which this member is reduced than the others.
But if it is excused upon you and does not obey the entrance with this species of cure of all, then take hold of the two legs of the patient together with a strong, light bandage, on both the ankles and both the knees.
And the length of each of its parts is the quantity of four digits, and the leg of the patient extended more than the other by the quantity of two digits.
And then the patient is suspended over the head of the pole, and that it is in the middle; and the length of him from the ground is the quantity of two arms.
And then command a strong young man to pull the head of the thigh, and that it is suspended with the patient another young man, and the other young man pulls the thigh with strength and impulsion, for the joint returns to its place with speed.
But in the proper reduction, when the dislocation is in the outer part, then the patient should lie on his back as we have recounted in the having gelbozitat; and be tightened the bandage on the leg of the patient properly and on the feet of him.
And then two poles should be placed, one at his feet, and the other at his head; and then poles adjusted in the middle of the bed, on which damp cloths should be wrapped, so that the patient is not harmed because the pole is between his thighs, for that the extension to the inner parts is not pulled.
And then each minister extends to his part, and the doctor with his hand encircles the reduction according to the art.
And when the dislocation is in the front parts, then the leg should be extended slightly, and it is according to this same narration about bed; and the doctor places the palm of his right hand on the shoulder of the patient, and then pulls that with the other hand, and with that pulling pauses that extended to the inner parts to the part of the knee.
And if the dislocation is in the back parts, then it is not necessary for the patient to be extended to the inner parts, and it is elevated on the ground; it should be placed on a hard cause, as it is necessary for the eyssament if the width of him is dislocated in the outer parts, according to what we have said of the jasement of him on two widths; and it is on his face and the bandages are extended, as we have said, there is no harm.
And it should be administered compression with a board on the place where the joint is.
Therefore, as the reduction is complicated according to what is necessary — the sign of the reduction of him is not hidden from you, and it is that you extend from the patient two legs, and when you see those enguals and the patient extends his leg and expands that ses excusacio, then you know that the member according to what is necessary has returned — and then you adjust two bandages and pause plaster and extend with bandage so that the width is not harmed in any of the parts; and adhere the patient to rest for three days or for four.
And then untie the bandage and the plaster, and compare one leg with the other.
Now, if you see those joints in alignment, then you know the dislocation is already fixed, and therefore let the patient go.
And if you see any cause for softening, then you return and plaster that, and extend that according to your first structure, and leave it for three days.
And then unwrap that, and make that person delay walking for a few days, until it is comforted.
Chapter .xxxii.
Of the cure of dislocation of the shoulder.
The shoulder is dislocated in three ways, which is dislocated to the outside parts, and to the inside parts, and to the parts in front to the back parts; and to the front parts it is not dislocated.
And the sign of dislocation of it is that you command the patient to apply their leg to their thigh; then you know that the shoulder is dislocated.
And the restoration of all the ways of it is that you make the patient straight, so that he already extends his leg, if he can over that; adhere your two to the face of it, and place his foot between your feet; and then make adhere the shoulder of it to your palms, and keep those between your fingers on the shoulder of it with strength, and another minister extends his leg while the shoulder returns to its place.
And the sign of the return of it is that his leg adheres to the thigh with lightness without labor.
And then plaster that and make the leg adhere to the thigh, and then tie those together immediately with a bandage for three days or for four, and then unwrap those.
And do not use the patient to walk for a few days, until it is healed and comforted.
But if the reduction of it to you is excused, then administer strong extension with ligaments of which in the cure of the hernia preceding narration.
Chapter .xxxiii.
Of the cure of the dislocation of the ankle.
The ankle some times is dislocated by slight movement, and some times is dislocated according to complement, and the dislocation of it is made either to the inside parts or to the outside parts.
And the sign of the dislocation of it is that you see the ankle inflated proceeding to the part to which it is dislocated.
But the cure of the dislocation of it is of slight reduction, and it is that it be extended with ease with the hands and be aligned while it returns.
But in the cure of it when it is dislocated according to complement, cover that you make the patient straight, and have that one minister strong and valiant of the part behind the two of it in the middle location of it.
And then you with your right hand the foot of the most sovereign part, and with your left hand of the part most below of the foot in the location of the ankle.
And then you pull the foot to you with your right hand, and with the left two times, and then extend with the left; and push the foot of the foot with the right towards the thigh that the leg works.
And do this two times according to that we have counted.
And then push the foot of the foot to the thigh the third time, and you are at the ankle.
Therefore if it returns in one time or in two according to this manner, and if you see the foot aligned, it is good; and if not, then over it iterates the operation, for that it returns.
But if to you is forbidden the reduction of it with that which we have recounted, then make the patient lie on his two on the ground, and stretch a padded cloth on the ground firm, and that it lies between the thighs of it, and you already have enveloped over it cloth so that it does not hurt the patient.
And then the minister of it holds its thighs, and another minister extends the leg with its hands or with ligaments that lie on the collar of the foot; and then extend that each minister against extension of its part, and the cloth be extant between the thighs of the patient holding it, so that the body of it not be pulled to the parts below according to its extension.
And then the physician aligns the dislocation with its hands, and another minister holds the healthy thigh to the parts below, for the dislocation returns with ease.
And therefore when the dislocation returns and is declared to you the health of the reduction of it, then pause plaster and extend that with ligaments strongly, and tie the foot with ligaments to the thigh.
And cover that you fear or guard yourself from the nerves which are behind on the ankle, so that the ligament over it not be vehement and hurt it strongly.
And then leave that for two days or three; and if the ligament is softened, extend that.
And then unwrap that on the third day or on the fourth, and prohibit the patient from movement for forty days. But if it is forced to go before that space, it is not done with safety that the dislocation not be over it dissolved and corrupted, and then that which does not receive cure.
And if it happens to it an abscess caut, then cover that you administer in the cure of it that in the place of our narration, in another place of cure and embrocation, until it is healed.
Chapter .xxxiiii.
Of the cure of dislocation of the toes.
So that the one that is dislocated be straightened with little extension of its work; and that which is not difficult, lift it lightly.
But if the dislocation is in some joints of the foot, then make the patient place his foot on a level surface of the earth or on a table, and standing thus as if he were walking.
And then stand near the patient, and place your foot upon what is prominent of the joints, and then press that with your foot with virtue until it returns, and that you see it already straightened and does not appear in the prominence.
And then place under the foot of the patient a table that supports the whole foot, which has two heads, and then strengthen that with a decent and firm structure for three days; and then untie that and make the patient abstain from walking for many days, until it is strengthened and its return is assured.
Chapter .xxxv.
Of the kinds of dislocations that are made with plague or with fracture or with any one of these together.
When accidents happen from any of those causes, and you are engaged in the cure and restoration of it, many times the death occurs.
And for this reason, do not presume over the cure of it, but he who is wise in the art, of long usage, merciful and compassionate, tardy, not bold nor presumptuous; and that uses in the beginning of medicines that cause pus, only so much, and leaves the patient to the divine judgment, but to him whom you hope for health from peril, with the alleviation of the sickness, and in which you see some hope. And therefore, strive as soon as possible to make the reduction of it at the beginning of the cause, before it becomes suppurating.
And therefore, if the limb returns as we wish, then administer a regimen which causes pus and cures the plague with what is convenient for it from the dried herbs.
And if the dislocation is with a fracture and happens in the bones separated, then you pierce the stem of them, and do in that what we have said in the simple ailments of this that is preceded in the places of those.
And guard and avoid according to your virtue that of the entrance in the ways of fear according to what has preceded you my preaching; for this is better, you owe your Creator, and more permanent to your glory, and more greetings to your true body in your time. Thus ends the words of Albucasim perfectly of which God be the benefit. Amen.
